0446310786|5.0|When I was 14 years old, I was a typical teenage boy of the times. Reading was more of a drudgery than it was an enjoyment. Then, I entered my freshman year and God's providence placed me under the guidance of an English teacher named Mrs. Lemke. She had an uncanny ability of matching students up with just the right reading assignments. A few weeks into my freshman year, after she had gotten to know her students, she assigned me two books, WATERSHIP DOWN and TO KILL A MOCKINGBIRD, to read and report on. When I learned that one was about rabbits and the other, a little girl, I was furious. The least she could have done would be to give me westerns or war stories. Eventually, I conceded to the fact that the two books would have to be read and so began my journey into a life long love of books.  I credit those two books with totally changing my outlook or reading for the sake of enjoyment. What a brilliant teacher Mrs. Lemke proved to be and I thank God for putting her in my life.<br /><br />That was over 30 years ago and I would venture to say, I have read Harper Lee's TO KILL A MOCKINGBIRD probably 15 times.  It's one of those rare volumes that you just have to take down off the shelf, dust it off and re-acquaint yourself with its brilliant narrative. I just consider it a travesty that Harper Lee wrote only this one single masterpiece. She had such a way of luring the reader into a love affair with her subjects.<br /><br />The story of Atticus Finch and his two children, Jem and Scout, or Jean Louise as she so detested being called, encompasses so many of life's lessons and virtues. We read as the children struggle with their father's identity, racial tension, social differences and a neighbor shrouded in mystery and myth. We romantically consider their world \\"simpler times\\", but to these two children and there good friend, Dill, they seemed anything but simple. And the portrait of their father, Atticus, is so magnificently portrayed by the author as a bastion of virtue. There should be a little bit of Atticus Finch in all of us.<br /><br />These days, I don't read much fiction, but this old favorite comes down every couple of years to be enjoyed over and over, and I can honestly say, with each reading, I enjoy it as much as ever. Thank you Harper Lee, for giving us this treasure, and thank you Mrs. Lemke for changing my life.<br /><br />Monty Rainey<br />[...]d be a little bit of Atticus Finch in all of us. B00005JO04|2.0|Here is a movie I was really excited to see and really wanted to like.  It had all the elements of many of my favorite films, not the least which was topical plot and a cast a crew with a diverse and respected pedigree.  Add to this generally glowing reviews by most of the country's \\"name\\" critcs, and \\"Syriana\\" looked to be a can't miss; a searing political thriller filled with twists and suspense and eye-opening facts on war, corruption and big business.  That's at least what the reviews and the film's trailer (literaly) promissed.      What the forces-that-be behind \\"Syriana\\" have infact delivered is a great trailer and premise in search of an actual movie.  I almost feel cheated and lied to.  The movie I was promised is not what turns up on screen.  It is one thing to not have your expectations met because you didn't really understand what kind of movie you were bellying up for, it is another to be dumbfounded because a movie was promoted to be a bookend to a movie like \\"Traffic,\\" turns out to be something more akin to watching 2 hours of CNN analysist bicker back and forth, yet all be in agreement of what the others are saying.  There were a few critics who slammed this movie, but I think most of the one's who praised it didn't understand it or know what to make of it, but they knew the movie must have been importaint because it was about big, importaint issues, so at the risk of looking like they didn't get it, they praised it as being as great and importaint a movie as the people invovled obviously thought it was (lest they risk looking foolish if the movie garnered all the awards and attention a movie like this can garner, but not surprisingly, didn't).      The truth is, \\"Syriana\\" is the film equivelent of washing your dishes before putting them in the dishwasher:  It is a lot of extra work (to get to the same outcome either way) and ultimately pointless.  This movie begins with a rather straight forward story and then piles on characters, b-stories and characters with b-stories (what was the deal with the Matt Damon character and his family?) and then ends up right where it began with no one any the wiser for all the trouble; least of all the audience.  This film demands attention, and a good film that rewards the attention paid in the end deserves it.  But this movie puts you through the ringer trying to keep with what's going on; you're never sure you get it or if it makes sense (not your fault as a dumb viewer mind you, but the writters'; its one thing to say pay attention, it is another to expect us to make sense of something that, as written, makes no sense).  In the end many of the stories connect, but as a viewer this does not make for any kind of brilliant catharsis; you get it, but you're left thinking, 'so what?'  The finale would like to be thought of as shocking or tragic, or something that leaves the audience with something to think about, but it feels, not only anticlimatic, but after working so hard to follow what was being said and done, it just wasn't worth the trouble.  That hardly follows the rule of rewarding the audience for having had to decode everything that lead up to that point.      I'd be willing to wager someone could watch the first 15 minutes of this movie and the last five and come away with the same message and understaning of what the film is trying to get across; which could also be summed up in a sentece or two by any one involved in the film.      \\"Syriana\\" comes off as a long, overblown journey to nowhere.  You can't fault the actors or the director - they no what they are doing, but someone should have put the script through a serious rewrite.  This film is so muddled it is almost completely incoherent.  It is obviously well-meaning in its mission statement; and its thesis is strong, but the way in which the movie sets out to prove its point (a point that really needs no actual \\"proving;\\" it's a fact that some of these type of events occur, so what's the point?), all it really does is preach to the choir; and that's if the choir even gets that they are being preached to. B000E6UK5K|4.0|It took a while, but I have FINALLY decided that I like the third David Gilmour album very much. Many seem to be measuring the work against the second Gilmour solo album, \\"About Face.\\" That probably is the best way to go about reviewing \\"On an Island\\" because I feel that the first Gilmour album is an under-appreciated master work. I would put this new one ahead of \\"About Face.\\"     Some of the criticism offered on these pages is valid. There does seem to be some repetition in Gilmour's riffs in some places, as one reviewer noted, though many of the repeated patterns are signature Gilmour such as the multi-step bends and the whammy pedal slides. I agree completely with the assessment that in order to appreciate this album fully, one will likely need to listen to it multiple times. I have listened to it four or five times, also. I was disappointed the first time around, as well. The melodies really start to come together during the second and third listens, however; then the subtleties of the compositions become gradually more apparent.    My favorite tracks are the title track, which is among Gilmour's best-ever solo compositions, \\"A Pocket Full of Stones,\\" \\"Then I Close My Eyes,\\" and \\"Red Sky at Night.\\" \\"The Blue,\\" \\"Smile,\\" \\"Where We Start\\" and \\"This Heaven\\" are also nice. \\"Take a Breath\\" is my least favorite, although it does have some great steel guitar work -- surpise, surprise.    The collection is very moody and relaxing. You may fall asleep around the middle of the album -- a criticism in the text on Amazon that is NOT valid. The track most likely to induce sleep is entitled \\"Then I Close My Eyes,\\" after all! On an Island is a very quiet album. Quiet albums are relaxing!     The editorial reviewer on Amazon mentioned that \\"This Heaven\\" ventures into unexpected territory with its R&B feel. The statement is absolutely ridiculous given that Gilmour has always been a couple of guitar effects away from being a blues guitarist! The reviewer's use of the term R&B isnot entirely incorrect. The term as it is used today is different than the traditional usage -- \\"blues\\" used to be a much more prominent aspect of R&B. However, straight \\"blues\\" describes the song more suitably.      I would like to say regarding a certain reviewer's musical \\"equation,\\" in which \\"lyrical content\\" was said to be an essential element of music, that instrumentals have NO \\"lyrical content.\\" Therefore, \\"lyrical content\\" is NOT essential to great music. Are the countless instrumental classical compositions and soundtracks not music? Hey, here's an idea! Let's all pull out an AC/DC album and listen to the lyrics! How about a Van Halen album? Now THAT'S deep! Do I hate AC/DC & Van Halen because of their \\"lyrics\\"? NO! They are in-your-face rock 'n' roll bands! Lyrics are a BONUS!     The opinions regarding the lyrics on \\"On an Island\\" seem to be mixed, as far as I can tell. I think the words are fine -- very moving at times, especially those of the title track. They work very well with the music. They are NOT all about happy themes, either, which is not to say that lyrics have to be sad in order to be good.    Yet another reviewer compared the songs on \\"On an Island\\" to some on \\"Meddle.\\" While I can understand the \\"A Pillow of Winds\\" comparison\\", possibly even the \\"Cirrus Minor\\" one to an extent, I must point out that the latter is on the \\"More\\" soundtrack, not \\"Meddle.\\"    One song \\"On an Island\\" brings to mind for me is an obscure Floyd track, often called \\"Rain in the Country\\" -- a trimmed-down version appears on the Zabriskie Point soundtrack under a different title -- \\"Then I Close My Eyes\\" seems to have a similar feel (without the blues part). \\"Poles Apart,\\" from \\"The Division Bell,\\" has a number of the atmospheric characteristics present on this new album. When I first heard \\"The Blue,\\" I immediately thought of the Alan Parsons Project song from his Edgar Allan Poe album entitled \\"To One in Paradise.\\" Some of the same impressions I had upon hearing \\"Obscured by Clouds\\" are here, also; although I was more immediately enthusiastic about The Valley soundtrack than \\"On an Island.\\" My enthusiasm has definitely grown, however.    \\"On an Island\\" is a very thoughtful, beautiful, and emotional album. Give it a chance, and you will find yourself listening to it again and again. The album should easily withstand the test of time.    Oh yes...why do you narrow-minded Waters fans keep buying, or at least listening to David Gilmour albums, anyway? You guys ARE smart, aren't you?

I'm no fan of slash-gash-scream-gore type films, but when the terror is part of a tapestry most delicately woven, a piece that is subtle and blatant, a love story and a horror story, a gripping and shocking piece where the opening of a door becomes a  moment of nail-biting tension... then it's not a slash-film but a film of art.<br /><br />\\"Nosferatu\\" has been described as the greatest horror film of all time. I cannot disagree - Murnau's remarkable use of double-negatives and his various lighting techniques impart such a wonderful sense of the macabre to this film. The acting varies - the young estate agent is no Olivier, but oh mon Dieu... oh, Max Schreck... what a superb performance his Graf Orlock is.<br /><br />It's the creepiest performance of a vampire that has ever been seen. The makeup is wonderful - the atmosphere is wonderful - the truly frightening creature who is almost uncontrollable at the sight of fresh blood is wonderful in a grisly sense.<br /><br />This is a film not to be missed. Whether you are a fan of the horror genre or not, Nosferatu is a classic in film-making.
B000E6UK5K|5.0|I shouldn't be shocked that some here have really trashed this album.  Everyone is entitled to their opinion, and my opinion of them is that they are obtuse and incapable of accepting anything that doesn't sound like The Wall or DSOTM.  Get over it people.  Those amazing albums will never even come close to being duplicated.  David brings us a super smooth, and super mellow album.  He is an aging rocker, and like many of his contemporaries he has produced a solo album that isn't injected with 30 year old testosterone-laden songs.  It is well arranged and has rich textures and soundscapes, and David's voice is as smooth as ever.  Polly does fine work on the lyrics, contrary to what others here have said about them.  I agree that when David and Roger worked together, they were a perfect example of the whole being much bigger than the individual parts.  But so what.  That Floyd magic lives on, but will never be equalled again.  So enjoy this album for what it is...no delusions of grandeur, no attempts to slide a fast one past anybody.  It is a personal endeavor for Gilmour and for those who enjoy it will enjoy it immensely.  For those who don't (there will always be the few), too bad for your close-mindedness.  Looking forward to seeing you, David, in Chicago in April!
